# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

I found **14 C++ source files** that implement HTTP connection manager route matching, organized into these categories:

### **Core Components:**

1. **HTTP Connection Manager Configuration** (2 files)
   - `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h|cc`
   - Creates and configures HCM filter with route matching

2. **Route Configuration & Matching** (2 files)
   - `source/common/router/config_impl.h|cc`
   - Implements the complete route matching algorithm with:
     - **RouteMatcher**: Virtual host selection (exact, wildcard-suffix, wildcard-prefix, default)
     - **VirtualHostImpl**: Route matching within virtual host (matcher tree + legacy routes)
     - **CommonVirtualHostImpl**: Shared virtual host configuration
     - **Multiple RouteEntryImpl types**: Path matchers (prefix, exact, regex, URI template, etc.)

3. **Router Filter** (2 files)
   - `source/common/router/router.h|cc`
   - HTTP filter that invokes route matching and dispatches to upstream

4. **Dynamic Route Configuration** (4 files)
   - RDS/VHDS implementation for dynamic route updates
   - Scoped routes for advanced routing scenarios

5. **Route Config Providers** (4 files)
   - Static and dynamic route configuration management

matching\\n   - Runtime matching\\n5. **Route Action Dispatch**:\\n   - Get cluster from matched route entry\\n   - Apply retry policies\\n   - Apply header transformations\\n   - Forward request to upstream\\n\\n## Key Matching Features\\n\\n- **Virtual Host Matching**: Domain-based routing with wildcard support and port-aware matching\\n- **Path Matching**: Multiple algorithms (prefix, exact, regex, URI template, path-separated-prefix)\\n- **Header Matching**: Match on request headers (case-insensitive or case-sensitive)\\n- **Method Matching**: HTTP method filtering\\n- **Query Parameter Matching**: Match query parameters in URL\\n- **Runtime Matching**: Configuration-driven feature flags\\n- **Matcher Tree**: Complex conditional matching for advanced scenarios\\n- **Direct Response**: Generate responses without routing to backend\\n- **SSL/TLS Requirements**: Enforce HTTPS based on virtual host configuration\\n\\nThis comprehensive implementation provides Envoy with a flexible, high-performance route matching system that supports both simple domain/path-based routing and complex conditional matching scenarios.\\n\"\n}\n",
